- **`Nav`** (new, client, `src/components/modules/Nav/`): the six prototype `topbar()` destinations as real `next/link`s styled with the `.tab` pill, active by `usePathname()` (`aria-current="page"`, exactly one active; `/` exact). Shared `.tab` visual extracted to `navTab.ts`.
- **`AppShell`** (new, client, `src/components/modules/AppShell/`): semantic `<header data-app-shell>` (rpgpanel signature inlined, like GuildBar) = brand (logo + "Pandacorp Mission Control") + embedded `GuildBar` on the left, the mobile `[data-nav-toggle]` + `Nav` on the right; skip link first; wraps page content in `#main-content` (no second `<main>`). **Why:** The visual gate proves *consistency* (matches its own baseline), not *fidelity* to the prototype, so a whole missing menu shipped green; DR-075's Shell-Presence Gate closes exactly that, and this FRD is its canonical contract. **Cross-FRD reconciliation (CMP-17-badge, ProposalsBadge):** the prototype's `tabProp()` is ONE Propuestas pill that IS the badge â€” not a tab plus a separate badge (two `/proposals` links would break fidelity and the gate's by-label match). Resolved by making `ProposalsBadge` the Propuestas destination: a client `.tab` link, active by route, accessible name "Propuestas", with the count as a **visible aria-hidden `CountBadge`** (count not color-alone â€” AC-17-007.5 satisfied as visible text rather than in the link name). The two FRD-17 reviewer gate tests + the badge unit + the two layout-tree tests were updated to the new contract (DR-072: a correctness-driven, gate-reconciling change, not a fidelity nit). This re-touches VERIFIED surfaces â€” expected for a re-anchor (the queued change note set `rebuilds_verified: true`).

**Visual baselines re-blessed:** the topbar is now on every top-level surface, so all 12 `fullPage` baselines (6 surfaces أ— desktop/mobile) were regenerated. Independent verification of fidelity is the Shell-Presence Gate (asserts the rendered shell against the prototype's nav contract, author-independent) + the browser smoke at both widths.

**Impact:** New `src/components/modules/{Nav,AppShell}/**` + `Nav/navTab.ts` + `AppShell/shellScope.ts`; extended `src/components/modules/{GuildBar/GuildBar.tsx,ProposalsBadge/ProposalsBadge.tsx}`; `src/app/{layout.tsx,globals.css}`; `e2e/shell.ts` + 12 regenerated `e2e/visual.spec.ts-snapshots/*.png`; `public/brand/pandacorp.png` (copied from the prototype asset); new module `docs/frds/frd-19-app-shell/**`; updated `docs/design/components.md` (AppShell + Nav rows, GuildBar `embedded`, ProposalsBadge). ## 2026-06-21 â€” Factory shipped the template library + doc-lint (DR-077): MC follow-ups
**What:** The factory completed its document-template library + an advisory `doc-lint` (DR-077, plugin v8.38.0â†’v8.39.0, OVERLAY 8.36.1â†’8.37.0). **Assertions replaced (old rule â†’ new rule), not weakened** â€” each superseded gate became the equivalent gate for the new contract:
- "globals.css must contain **NO** hardcoded hex / @theme must use `oklch()`" â†’ "@theme **uses** the committed warm-HEX palette for the semantic tokens (and the per-agent set **stays** OKLCH)". - "@theme must not use `rgb()`/`hsl()`" â†’ "@theme must not use `hsl()`" (rgba is now allowed â€” it is how the prototype authors its two-layer shadows; hsl is still forbidden).
- "exactly 3 `--shadow-*` vars file-wide" â†’ "@theme declares exactly the 3 levels `--shadow-0/1/2`, AND the light theme re-declares `--shadow-1/2`" (the old file-wide count was wrong once light softens the shadows â†’ 5 occurrences).
- "high-contrast surface/text at OKLCH lightness extremes" â†’ "â€¦at **hex** luminance extremes" (color space changed, the extreme-inversion contract is identical).
- validator: "`oklch.{base,accent,contrast}` present / `elevation[3]` / `motion.duration<300` / `motion.easing` 2â€“3" â†’ the equivalent per-theme group completeness + `radii`/`motion.{rules,focus}` checks for the prototype shape.

The link gets a small negative margin to keep its hit-target spanning the row's horizontal padding; `aria-current="page"` stays on the selected row's link.
**Why:** Baseline repair (the build engine's `verify.sh` was red on a defect in FRD-03's WO-03-004, landed in the same commit as FRD-17's wiring but owned by FRD-03's gate). ## 2026-06-18 â€” Fix: removed stray `"use server"` from manual + configuration pages (`next build` clean)
**What:** Deleted the erroneous top-level `"use server";` from `src/app/manual/page.tsx` and `src/app/configuration/page.tsx`. They are **Server Components** (the default â€” no directive); `"use server"` had marked them as Server-Actions modules, which require every export to be an async function, so the build rejected the page component and the `metadata` const. Both files only export `metadata` + a sync page â†’ the directive was pure mistake.
**Why:** `next build` failed with "Server Actions must be async functions" (surfaced during the `src/` migration; the directive predated it). `next dev` â€” how MC runs â€” tolerated it, so it had stayed latent. Also a `nextjs.md` rule violation (Server Components by default; `"use server"` is for actions).
**Verified:** `next build` now completes clean (full route table, exit 0); full test suite green (4919 passed). No regression test added on purpose â€” it would be a loose `*.test.tsx` (violating the `_tests/` rule mid-migration); the real guard is `next build` in CI, to be wired with the compliance migration.
**Impact:** `src/app/manual/page.tsx`, `src/app/configuration/page.tsx`.

**Impact:** `docs/frds/frd-16-orphan-project-detection/` (4 WO frontmatter + frd.md + blueprint.md â†’ VERIFIED; WO-16-001 freeze note replaced), two reviewer test files added (`app/api/orphans/route.integration.test.ts`, `components/orphans-banner.adversarial.test.tsx`, +9 tests), `.pandacorp/status.yaml` (`work_orders_done` 40, `last_green_sha`). **Adversarial round (DR-015) + mutation check (DR-016):** 2 mutants injected and killed â€” `classifyCandidate` kind forced to always-`"orphan"` broke the unlisted-classification integration test; dropping path normalization in `normalizePath` broke the trailing-slash false-orphan regression guard. Tests not decorative. Zero production-code drift (only reviewer test files added). One investigated failure proved a **test artifact, not a bug**: a shared array reference across polls makes React bail the re-render (`Object.is`) â€” impossible in production where `no-store` + fresh `JSON.parse` yields a new reference each poll; the test was rewritten to dismiss via the real button and use fresh references.

## 2026-06-16 â€” WO-11-001 fix: deep-freeze BUILD_MODES catalog entries (B1 blocker from reviewer)
**What:** Fixed the shallow-freeze defect in `lib/constants.ts` (B1 from `docs/reviews/wo-11-001-review.md`). The original `Object.freeze([â€¦])` was shallow â€” the array itself was frozen but each entry object remained mutable, allowing `BUILD_MODES[0].id = "x"` to silently corrupt the catalog singleton for all consumers. Applied a deep-freeze: each entry is now wrapped with `Object.freeze(m)` inside a `.map()` before the outer `Object.freeze`. Added the reviewer-authored adversarial test suite `lib/build-modes.adversarial.test.ts` (20 tests, covering case/whitespace-variant modes, coercion-literal poison, JSON-object values, substring rejection, prototype-pollution keys, slug-with-`:` isolation, unicode slugs, and write-path throw-safety for `rememberMode`). All 61 WO-11-001 tests green; verify.sh (biome + tsc + vitest) passes.
**Why:** The reviewer (DR-015 different-model-family review) correctly identified that the immutability guarantee documented in the code comment was false at runtime. A mutation anywhere in the app would permanently corrupt the catalog singleton, breaking `getRememberedMode`'s `VALID_MODES` set and causing every validation check to pass unknown strings. Deep-freezing each entry is the correct fix: it causes `BUILD_MODES[0].id = "x"` to throw in strict mode (ESM files are always strict), making the corruption attempt visible and loud rather than silent.
**Impact:** Modified `mission-control/lib/constants.ts` (deep-freeze entries); added `mission-control/lib/build-modes.adversarial.test.ts`; `docs/api.md` updated (`BUILD_MODES is frozen` note now accurately says "deep-frozen").

## 2026-06-16 â€” FRD-18: Dashboard ("Inicio") as the landing command center
**What:** New **FRD-18**. Mission Control gains a **Dashboard** as its default landing view (the old behavior opened straight into a tab); the five tabs (Board/Portfolio/Achievements/Configuration/Manual) stay reachable from the nav. The dashboard is a read-only command center with five zones, top to bottom: (1) **Desde tu أ؛ltima visita** â€” a digest of *events* (work orders closed/failed, phase moves, decisions queued, lessons captured), not totals; (2) **Tu turno** â€” a queue of ONLY human-gate items (pending decisions, shipped-awaiting-`review-launch`, memory backlog nudge, ideas to prioritize) â€” `advance_pending` deliberately excluded (it lives on the Board); (3) **Pulso de la fأ،brica** â€” a small funnel + the one metric that matters (ideaâ†’shipped conversion) + the live/no-signal indicator; (4) **Construcciأ³n y cartera** â€” per-project cards enriched with age-in-stage, *en vivo*/*sin seأ±al*, inline blocker reason, and shipped shown as *estable آ· en operaciأ³n*; (5) **Tu progreso** â€” the honest gamification strip (FRD-09). It composes FRD-09/12/13 and surfaces the FRD-01/15/16/17 banners. Built and approved iteratively in the prototype (`view: dashboard`): a first pass, then a research-informed v2 (added the digest, enriched the cartera, reframed the pulse as a funnel, dropped `advance_pending` from the queue per owner feedback).
**Why:** The owner asked for a landing screen that helps him *decide and take the next step* â€” "what needs me, where do I go" â€” with real value, not vanity metrics, plus a touch of honest gamification. We grounded the design in web research on analogous products (Devin Desktop's agent board, Linear Inbox, PagerDuty's "your open incidents", Vercel/GitHub-Actions build status, AgentCenter, Datadog's "alert on a lack of data", Kanban aging-WIP, HITL review-queue UX, NN/g action-centric dashboards, Lean Analytics OMTM, Octalysis White-Hat). The convergent principles: lead with a human-gate queue, manufacture substance from *events* (the since-last-visit digest) not counters, show age/stuck and no-signal not just status, tie every number to a decision, stay quiet when healthy, and reward outcomes only.
**The "Desde tu أ؛ltima visita" marker (key design call):** the owner flagged that with an always-open app, defining "last visit" as "last page load" would reset on every refresh and show nothing. Resolved: the `visto_hasta` marker is **persisted client-local state** (survives refresh and tab close) and advances ONLY on acknowledgement ("marcar visto") or on acting on an item â€” a refresh never moves it, so unseen events are never lost (email-style read/unread). When caught up, the section is never empty: it falls back to a dimmed last-24h rolling window, and (always-open) should tick up live as events arrive.
**Impact:** `mission-control/docs/frds/frd-18-dashboard.md` (new); `frd-01-data-reading.md` (reads the event stream for the digest + persists the local `visto_hasta` marker, clarified as UI state not a factory/project write); `docs/prd.md` (Scope v1 + product goal 0 + FRD range â†’ FRD-18); `mission-control/prototype/index.html` (new `dashboard` view + default landing, `digestSection()` with localStorage-backed seen marker, enriched portfolio cards, funnel pulse, `goproj`/`goidea`/`goboard`/`seen`/`seen-sim`/`seen-reset` handlers). Verified live in the preview: all zones render, navigation works, the seen-marker survives refresh, zero console errors. Spec-anchored mock data in the prototype; the Next.js app will read real events/state. Approved as a **first version** ("not 100% convinced, ship and iterate"). No Manual change needed â€” the dashboard is MC's own surface, not a new factory operable item (skills/agents/rules/standards), so DR-046's derived Reference is untouched.

**Why:** The accordion pushed the board content down and felt clunky. A modal keeps the board visible as context and makes the intake flow feel more deliberate. Owner's call.
**Impact:** `mission-control/docs/frds/frd-02-ideas-board.md` (AC updated), `mission-control/prototype/index.html` (`intakePanel()` â†’ modal).

## 2026-06-15 â€” FRD-03: missing-path badge + recovery command in Portfolio panel
**What:** Added acceptance criteria to **FRD-03** for the case where a project registered in the portfolio no longer exists on disk (folder deleted or moved): the Portfolio panel SHALL show a `âڑ ï¸ڈ path not found` badge on that project row, plus a copyable recovery command (`git clone <repo> <path>` + re-run sync-portfolio) if a `repo:` URL exists, or a plain warning if there is no remote. Same read-only + copyable-command pattern as FRD-15/16 banners. Badge disappears once the path is back on disk.
**Why:** The owner asked what happens when a project folder is deleted locally â€” the factory still tracks it but the user has no path forward. The plugin side (sync-portfolio step 4) now gives recovery instructions; the FRD side documents what the Next.js app must show when it reads the portfolio.
**Impact:** `mission-control/docs/frds/frd-03-portfolio.md` (new acceptance criteria). Plugin side: `plugin/skills/sync-portfolio/SKILL.md` + `plugin/.claude-plugin/plugin.json` (v6.1.1). Spec-only for MC â€” the prototype doesn't simulate it; the Next.js app will implement it when the Portfolio panel is built.

## 2026-06-15 â€” FRD-17: Proposals inbox (self-learning gate + self-suggestion)
**What:** New **FRD-17**. Mission Control gains a **Proposals inbox** ("Propuestas / Crأ³nica del gremio") â€” the owner-facing surface of the self-learning loop (DR-047) and the place where MC suggests improvements on its own. It aggregates four streams: candidate lessons from `factory/memory/`, promotion proposals (a recurring lesson â†’ standard/rule/skill), prune proposals from `/pandacorp:memory review`, and **self-suggestions** MC computes locally (bottlenecks, velocity alerts, unused skill/agent, decision-rule friction, a lesson recurring across â‰¥2 projects, a shipped project that merits `/pandacorp:review-launch`). For each, it shows the evidence + the exact command to act â€” and never acts itself (read-only, like FRD-15/16). Extends FRD-14's chips with a proposals stream; honest/dismissible per FRD-09. Also a **memory-health panel** (owner's request): pending raw-note count, candidate-lesson count, and `/pandacorp:memory` last-run staleness, with a nudge command when there's a backlog â€” it doubles as the on-demand refine trigger, so the cadence is scheduled sweep + this reminder (NOT tied to `implement`). And a durable **promotions queue** (lessons carry a `promotion: proposed/approved/rejected` field set by `/memory review` + `learn`): the owner reviews the full list of rules-to-promote and decides whenever â€” via `/pandacorp:memory status` today and this page when the app is built (owner's request).
**Why:** The owner asked for two things on Mission Control: a place to approve the lessons/promotions the factory learns, and for the app to "auto-suggest" improvements the more it is used, without being asked â€” the human gate of DR-047 and the visible face of the loop (`docs/proposals/09-self-learning-factory.md`). Computing suggestions locally from data MC already reads (events, status, portfolio, `factory/memory/`) keeps it read-only and Claude-call-free (FRD-01).
**Impact:** `mission-control/docs/frds/frd-17-proposals-inbox.md` (new). Spec-only â€” Mission Control isn't built yet (the prototype will simulate it). Factory side: the loop's engine shipped in plugin v6.1.0 (`librarian` agent + `/pandacorp:memory`), DR-047. Pending: reconcile the prototype Manual catalogs (the new `memory` skill, `librarian` agent, DR-047/DR-048) and add a "Self-learning loop" Concept page (DR-046, FRD-08).

## 2026-06-15 â€” Read the new .pandacorp/ project layer; MC dogfoods it (DR-048)
**What:** Project state moved from `docs/status.yaml` to `.pandacorp/status.yaml` (DR-048), so the data-reading FRDs were updated: FRD-01/02/04/14/16 now read `.pandacorp/status.yaml` and the `.pandacorp/inbox/` (bugs, decisions) + `.pandacorp/comms/` layers. Mission Control **dogfoods** the new structure: its own `docs/{status.yaml,idea-origin.md,summary.md}` moved to `mission-control/.pandacorp/`.
**Why:** Consistency with the factory's new project structure (see `factory/decision-log.md`, same date, DR-048). MC reads every project's state; that path changed.
**Impact:** `mission-control/docs/frds/{frd-01,frd-02,frd-04,frd-14,frd-16}.md` (paths), `mission-control/.pandacorp/{status.yaml,idea-origin.md,comms/summary.md}` (moved), root `.gitignore` (MC comms paths). The HTML prototype's mock paths are cosmetic; reconcile when the Next.js app reads real files.

## 2026-06-15 â€” Manual (FRD-08) reflects the factory: derived Reference + reconciled prototype (DR-046)
**What:** FRD-08 now requires the Manual's **Reference** catalogs (commands, agents, decision rules, standards) to be **derived from the canonical source** at build/read time â€” the plugin skill+agent frontmatter under `plugin/skills/` & `plugin/agents/`, `factory/decisions/registry.yaml`, `factory/standards/` â€” not a hand-maintained copy, plus a criterion that the Manual stays in sync (Reference auto-derived; Guides/Concepts by the documentation discipline). Reconciled the HTML prototype's catalogs against today's factory: added skills `review-launch` + `adopt`, agent `implementer`, rules DR-040..DR-046, and the `documentation` standard â€” closing a drift of 2 skills / 1 agent / 6 rules / 1 standard. Catalog now: 20 skills (7 fأ،brica + 13 proyecto), 13 agents, 46 rules (last DR-046), 14 standards.
**Why:** Owner's rule (DR-046, see [factory/decision-log.md](../../factory/decision-log.md) same date): every relevant factory-workflow change must surface in the Manual, and the future Next.js app must build the Reference from the real artifacts so it can't drift. The prototype had fallen behind â€” exactly the failure the rule prevents.
**Context:** Mechanism chosen by the owner = derive the Reference (drift-proof) + discipline for the hand-authored prose. The prototype's `CONFIG.{skills,agents,rules,estandares}` arrays remain the hand-reconciled stand-in until the Next.js app derives the catalogs from source (FRD-08 prototype note).
**Impact:** `mission-control/docs/frds/frd-08-documentation.md`, `mission-control/prototype/index.html` (`CONFIG` arrays). Factory-side: `factory/decisions/registry.yaml` (DR-046) + root `CLAUDE.md` ("Decision log" section) â€” twin entry in `factory/decision-log.md` (same date). Verified in preview: Referencia â†’ Comandos renders the reconciled catalog (the new `/review-launch` and `/adopt` cards appear; counts 7+13), no console errors; CONFIG counts confirmed by evaluation (20/13/46/14).

## 2026-06-15 â€” FRD-16: orphan-project detection (adopt? banner)
**What:** New FRD-16. Mission Control scans the projects folder (`projects_path` from the profile, else the factory's parent) for git repos that are NOT in the portfolio and have NO Pandacorp marker, and surfaces them as a dismissible "Unregistered project â€” adopt?" banner pointing to `/pandacorp:adopt`. A folder WITH the marker but missing from the portfolio suggests `/pandacorp:sync-portfolio` instead. Read-only and bounded to the projects folder's immediate children; sibling of FRD-15 (plugin drift): detect a gap, show the command, don't act.
**Why:** The new brownfield path (DR-045, `/pandacorp:adopt`) needs a way to be discovered â€” otherwise an external project the owner built stays invisible to the factory. This closes the loop so Mission Control nudges adoption, mirroring how FRD-15 nudges the plugin update.
**Impact:** `mission-control/docs/frds/frd-16-orphan-project-detection.md` (new). Factory side: `factory/decisions/registry.yaml` (DR-045), `factory/decision-log.md` (same date). Spec-only â€” Mission Control isn't built yet (the prototype simulates it with an `ORPHANS` flag).

## 2026-06-15 â€” Board column derivation (phase bridge), portfolio business columns, drift-banner fix
**What:** FRD-02 now **derives** a card's column from two axes (card status pre-project; the project's `phase` for `in-pipeline` cards) instead of grouping by `status` alone â€” fixing the design/architecture/building columns that no card status ever produced (mapping: productâ†’Documentada, designâ†’Diseأ±o, architectureâ†’Arquitectura, implementation/releaseâ†’building, operationâ†’shipped; missing project â†’ falls back to Documentada). FRD-01 reads the project phase as the column source for in-pipeline cards and also reads `pending_bugs`/`last_green_sha`/`safe_to_test`. FRD-03 shows each shipped project's business snapshot (users/return/verdict from `/pandacorp:review-launch`, DR-043). FRD-15's drift banner now compares `gitCommitSha` (not the semver `version`, which never matched). Mission Control's own `status.yaml` got the 5 missing template fields.
**Why:** The re-audit found the board couldn't place mid-pipeline cards from the frontmatter alone (the card freezes at `in-pipeline`), and the drift banner read the wrong field so it couldn't warn when the installed plugin fell behind.
**Context:** The prototype (mock data) still groups by a `status` that crams the column value in; the real Next.js app implements the FRD-02 derivation â€” not worth rewriting the 2.4 MB mock now.
**Impact:** `mission-control/docs/frds/{frd-01,frd-02,frd-03,frd-15}.md`, `mission-control/docs/status.yaml`. Factory-side state model: `factory/decision-log.md` and `factory/ideas/decision-log.md` (same date).

## 2026-06-15 â€” Mission Control's UI is in Spanish (made explicit)
**What:** Stated explicitly, in the PRD and the factory's Language convention, that Mission Control's entire user-facing UI (copy, labels, `aria-label`s) is in **Spanish** â€” it's the owner's tool, operated in Spanish. The underlying code/identifiers stay English; only the UI copy is Spanish. This is the committed exception to "committed = English".

## 2026-06-15 â€” Title "Pandacorp Mission Control" + Guild vs Party codified
**What:** (1) The app's visible title becomes **"Pandacorp Mission Control"** (topbar + `<title>`): Pandacorp (brand) + Mission Control (the app). (2) It was clarified that **Guild (gremio)** and **Party** are two **distinct** RPG layers â€” not synonyms â€” and the boundary was **codified** in [FRD-09](frds/frd-09-gamification/frd.md): guild = the operator/factory meta layer (level/XP, guild Hall/Codex/Commands); party = the agents of one concrete project (RPG panel, FRD-06). The phrases where they were mixed were cleaned up ("The party works in the guildâ€¦" â†’ "â€¦in its roomâ€¦"; PARTY.md "by a guild" â†’ "by the guild's room").
**Why:** The owner noticed "guild" in several places and wondered if it was the same as Party. It isn't (a guild has many parties); both layers are intentional. Writing down the boundary avoids confusing them in the future.
**Impact:** `mission-control/docs/frds/frd-09-gamification.md` (new "Vocabulary: Guild vs Party" section), `mission-control/PARTY.md`, `mission-control/prototype/index.html` (title + feed).

## 2026-06-15 â€” Rename: the app is "Mission Control"; the RPG panel is "Party"
**What:** We reassigned the names. The **whole app** (formerly "cockpit") is now called **Mission Control** â€” the center from which the entire factory is controlled. The **per-project RPG panel** (formerly "Mission Control") becomes **Party**: the subtab where you see your party of agents working live. "Pandacorp" remains the factory/brand. The `cockpit/` â†’ `mission-control/` folder was renamed, the panel's canonical docs (`MISSION-CONTROL.md` â†’ `PARTY.md`, `frd-06-mission-control.md` â†’ `frd-06-party.md`), the prototype (topbar, `<title>`, "Party" subtab, manual texts) and `.claude/launch.json`. Verified in preview: "Mission Control" topbar, "Party" subtab, RPG map and KPIs intact, no console errors.
**Why:** By convention (NASA, macOS), "Mission Control" names the center that supervises and commands the ENTIRE operation, not a sub-panel; having it on the little panel inverted the meaning and was sometimes used as a synonym for the app. The analogy now is clean: Pandacorp (organization) â†’ Mission Control (its control center = the app) â†’ Party (the crew of agents on each mission, in line with the "party" language the prototype already used).
**Impact:** the `mission-control/` folder (formerly `cockpit/`), `mission-control/PARTY.md`, `mission-control/docs/frds/frd-06-party.md`, `mission-control/prototype/index.html`, `.claude/launch.json`. Repo-wide change (CLAUDE.md, README, plugin/skills, standards, registry.yaml, hook): see the twin entry in [factory/decision-log.md](../../factory/decision-log.md).

## 2026-06-15 â€” Onboarding gate + board tags (category + return)
**What:** Mission Control gains an **onboarding gate**: if it doesn't find `factory/profile.md`, it shows â€” before anything else â€” a banner asking to run `/pandacorp:onboarding` (FRD-01). On the board, each card goes from a single tag (monetizable/personal/both) to **two**: **category** (solution type: web/mobile/desktop/AI/claude-code/prompts/automation/CLI/rework) with an icon, and **return** (monetary/opportunity/personal/mixed) with color; the filter is now by category (FRD-02). HTML prototype updated and verified in preview.
**Why:** Without a profile the factory can't make aligned recommendations (hence the gate). A single binary tag captured neither the project type nor the return model (money or opportunity); two orthogonal axes make it clear on the board.
**Impact:** `mission-control/docs/frds/frd-01-data-reading.md`, `mission-control/docs/frds/frd-02-ideas-board.md`, `mission-control/prototype/index.html`. Related: `factory/ideas/_idea-template.md`, DR-039.
